<div id="review_428007624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/428007624" />
    <a title="Jaime" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5687527-jaime"><img alt="Jaime" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419289339p2/5687527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/428007624?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime" href="/user/show/5687527-jaime">Jaime</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer428007624&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428007624" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2844508324067795529">The ending ruined it. Enough said.<br/><br/>ETA: Okay, it's been two days since I've finished this, and the more I think about it, the more annoyed I get. I feel like the last two books in the series might've spawned from ideas or even short stories that were set earlier in the series, and that the author took these ideas and reworked them into the last two novels to fill a contract or something. I hate to think that, but I felt like the quality of the writing went down in the last two novels. They were f</span>
  <span id="freeText2844508324067795529" style="display:none">The ending ruined it. Enough said.<br /><br />ETA: Okay, it's been two days since I've finished this, and the more I think about it, the more annoyed I get. I feel like the last two books in the series might've spawned from ideas or even short stories that were set earlier in the series, and that the author took these ideas and reworked them into the last two novels to fill a contract or something. I hate to think that, but I felt like the quality of the writing went down in the last two novels. They were filled with semi-pointless subplots (the Foaly-Caballine one, for example - it had nothing to do with the actual plot,) a lot of loose ends and a romantic subplot derailing, thanks to the old amnesia cliche. There was also a lot that only made sense if it had been taken from an earlier point in the series, or didn't make sense at all:<br /><br /><b>Artemis's death:</b> He was not a fairy. He only had a fairy eye. At worst, he should've lost the eye, rather than be killed entirely.<br /><br /><b>Artemis:</b> Artemis went from being a genius with a plan to being almost scared, weak and without ideas by the end. He almost seemed out of character.<br /><br /><b>Orion:</b> Disappeared. One is left to assume that simply vanished after Artemis's treatment - he's never mentioned again.<br /><br /><b>Butler:</b> After Butler's resurrection in The Eternity Code, he is said to be old on the inside and weak enough not to be able to bodyguard any longer. Yet, by the end of the series, he's as strong as he was in book one.<br /><br /><b>Juliet:</b> Juliet wished to become a pro-wrestler and seemed to be happy doing it. By book 8, though, she's become nothing more than a nanny/bodyguard to Myles and Beckett. She's not mentioned again after the berserkers leave.<br /><br /><b>Myles and Beckett:</b> Dropped. Myles simply goes to bed and Beckett is never mentioned again after the berserkers leave.<br /><br /><b>Mulch:</b> Goes from being friends with Artemis to robbing his house. This is something that makes me wonder if books 7 and 8 might've originally been written earlier in the series and pushed back. Mulch's personality in the last two books would've fit better after book one, rather than at the end.<br /><br /><b>No. 1:</b> Convienently absent from book 8, beyond a conversation with Holly. Another thing that makes me wonder if these novels were written out of order.<br /><br /><b>Nopal:</b> Hinted to possibly have a soul by Holly in the beginning, and then shown not to have anything at the end, which convienently allows for Artemis's resurrection. It seemed convienent and somewhat cruel.<br /><br /><b>Fowl Manor:</b> There really wasn't much explanation as to why the Fowl's were drawn to the fairy world, beyond the berserker's spiral being on their land. Maybe I missed something here, but I feel like there should've been some revelation here.<br /><br /><b>Opal Koboi:</b> A pixie with no magic blows herself up and then holds herself together by dark magic? I was totally confused here. Also, cold-blooded murder/execution seemed a little strong for the intended audience of these books.<br /><br />Yeah, there was just so many loose ends that I was honestly surprised this is the very last Artemis Fowl novel. There really needs to be another to clear everything up. Meh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2844508324067795529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3083032925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3083032925" />
    <a title="luna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/103916962-luna"><img alt="luna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578012383p2/103916962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3083032925?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="luna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="luna" href="/user/show/103916962-luna">luna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781368038836" href="/book/show/40143446-the-last-guardian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/103916962-luna?shelf=artemis-fowl">artemis-fowl</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3083032925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1997144837751152138">(A-) 90% | AGES 13+ | Ah...What is there to say about Artemis Fowl? The most cunning, clever, and intelligent boy alive and yet, somehow, still not the brightest. This was a good closure. But a closure to what? You might be wondering. So here are some questions I can answer in the end.<br/><br/>Should I read this series? <br/>To read Artemis Fowl is an acquired taste. If you like long chapters with multiple points of view and witty humor, this is for you. If you like goblins, fairies, daring exploits, time tra</span>
  <span id="freeText1997144837751152138" style="display:none">(A-) 90% | AGES 13+ | Ah...What is there to say about Artemis Fowl? The most cunning, clever, and intelligent boy alive and yet, somehow, still not the brightest. This was a good closure. But a closure to what? You might be wondering. So here are some questions I can answer in the end.<br /><br />Should I read this series? <br />To read Artemis Fowl is an acquired taste. If you like long chapters with multiple points of view and witty humor, this is for you. If you like goblins, fairies, daring exploits, time travel, demon possessions, and evil turned good characters, this is for you!<br /><br />Are the characters admirable? Something I can relate to on an emotional level?<br />Definitely! Artemis was an evil boy. He had done bad things in his life. Enough for a life sentence in only his first 12 years of age. Pretty soon, that guilt is going to catch up to him. I think we can all relate to the fact we’ve all been guilty before, and to see someone who’s trying to fix his mistakes, getting over his pride. That’s pretty relatable, and only the strongest of people can own up to it. Plus, like all people have the ability to receive, even if some seem too far gone, Artemis gets a redemption arc!<br /><br />Are the plots interesting? Enough to keep me reading all 8 books?<br />Oh! I think you shouldn’t entirely base the stories off of the first book. By the time you reach the fourth book, it’ll have you intrigued. But that is the fourth book. Luckily, these stories are pretty short. 2, 3, and 4 are pretty slow, but the last half of the books are pretty good. My personal favorite is the Time Paradox (#6). But if you don’t plan on reading all of them, reading the first book is a good taste tester.<br /><br />How is the writing? <br />It’s written in a clever way to reflect Artemis Fowl’s brain because it is so complex(but still teenager like). It’s written in multiple POV’s so you have time to get backstory from everyone, including villains. I did find the villain’s point of views kind of boring sometimes, and I sped-read to Artemis or Holly’s POV because they were more interesting. I’m not against the writing, just what it was about.<br /><br />So, what are my final thoughts?<br />Now, I judge my reviews solely on an emotional level and how much I’m going to remember this. Yes, there are some technical aspects, but I try not to get into that as much because I know how hard it is to write a book (lots of us do) and I respect every author for publishing their book and just finishing it in general. I think Colfer executed his vision for Artemis Fowl well. I’m going to remember this as something that faced ups and downs to me. The best review I can give you is in one sentence: “Artemis Fowl is an acquired taste, but once you have acquired it, it is a deliciously clever taste that will linger in your mouth for days and leave a flavorful sentimental after taste in the end.”<br /><br />Phew! My first time doing a long, thorough review like this! Just trying something different especially for the last book! Thanks Colfer for an amazing journey!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1997144837751152138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6525071911631984491" style="display:none">30/04/2020<br />3 ⭐<br />Unfortunately, I didn't *love* this book in the series either, but I loved every other book in the series, so I still count this as a win!     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2710461071" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2710461071" />
    <a title="Caylynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn"><img alt="Caylynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594527171p2/66237296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2710461071?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caylynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caylynn" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn">Caylynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2710461071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11593065184799457988"><i>3.75/5 stars</i><br/><i>
  <blockquote>Artemis Fowl, the human who had once lied as a matter of course, was surprised to find that in this instance, lying <b>for the greater good</b> did not make him feel any better about it.</blockquote>
</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505830378ra/23962520.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I DON'T KNOW HOW I FEEL ABOUT THIS FINAL INSTALLMENT.<br/><br/>I truly cannot figure out whether this was satisfying or not. I am absolutely certain now that I never read the final book in this series when it first came out, because I remember nothing that happened in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9307674.The_Last_Guardian__Artemis_Fowl___8_' title='The Last Guardian (Artemis Fowl, #8) by Eoin Colfer' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Last Guardian</a>.<br/><br/>There's pretty much everythi</span>
  <span id="freeText11593065184799457988" style="display:none"><i>3.75/5 stars</i><br><i>
  <blockquote>Artemis Fowl, the human who had once lied as a matter of course, was surprised to find that in this instance, lying <b>for the greater good</b> did not make him feel any better about it.</blockquote>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505830378ra/23962520.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I DON'T KNOW HOW I FEEL ABOUT THIS FINAL INSTALLMENT.<br><br>I truly cannot figure out whether this was satisfying or not. I am absolutely certain now that I never read the final book in this series when it first came out, because I remember nothing that happened in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9307674.The_Last_Guardian__Artemis_Fowl___8_" title="The Last Guardian (Artemis Fowl, #8) by Eoin Colfer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Guardian</a>.<br><br>There's pretty much everything in this book. Ancient berserker fairies that have been sleeping for ten thousand years, zombie pirates and Chinese warriors, death, Opal Koboi, possession, sieges, end-of-the-earth-as-we-know-it, global technological explosions and failures, etc. Did it all fit seamlessly well together? No. Did it all fit relatively <i>well</i> together? Definite Nope. I feel like there was too much going on, yet for some reason the whole body of the book was pretty much stagnant. <br><br>Don't get me wrong, there were plenty of good moments in the book. Myles and Beckett were adorable and snarky even when they were possessed by bloodthirsty warriors. We still got to see the main crew in action to the very end, leaving no one out for the count. There was still plenty of growth for some of the characters, even though this is the grand finale. I mean, Artemis is finally willing to make the <i>ultimate</i> sacrifice? WTF that definitely wouldn't have happened <i>anytime</i> in the first three books, maybe even the fourth book. <br><i>
  <blockquote>Artemis felt surprised at the finality of this step he was being forced to take- and also that he was willing to even consider taking it.<br><br>The boy who kidnapped Holly Short all those years ago would never have entertained the notion of scrificing himself.</blockquote>
</i><br>But, like, there's a certain point where a book can't solely rely on the same old "crew faces adversary-&gt;crew makes plan-&gt;plan doesn't go as expected-&gt;crew pulls another plan out of thin air-&gt;readers find out that that plan has been brewing for a long ass time-&gt;everything ends up okay." It just gets tiresome after a certain period of time, unless the author makes the "out of thin air" plan so damn elaborate and subtly present throughout the book that it blows my mind away. And in this book, it didn't work out that way for me. <br><br>Sure, I loved the ending that Artemis chose for himself, and I legitimately thought for a bit that that would be how the story ended. But to not give the readers closure and a chance to see how the decision he made affected the other characters is kind of poor writing. Not to mention everything is reversed on literally the <i>next page</i>. Just didn't vibe well with me. <br><br>And speaking of reversing things, there were a lot of OOC moments that grated on my nerves! Moments like the scene where Butler holds up a fist to signal STOP, and Artemis runs right into his back. We know with absolute certainty that Artemis already knows what this means, because he said so back in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37586.The_Lost_Colony__Artemis_Fowl___5_" title="The Lost Colony (Artemis Fowl, #5) by Eoin Colfer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Colony</a>. So why was this ass-backwards scene necessary? And then another one happens later in the book, where Holly realizes that Artemis is shutting down mentally because his plan didn't work. Apparently, if Artemis' "one and only Plan A" doesn't work, he flips out and doesn't know what to do?? What happened to the MULTIPLE CONTINGENCY PLANS THAT HE WAS ALWAYS PREPARED WITH IN THE FIRST LIKE FUCKING FOUR BOOKS?? Artemis has NEVER only relied on one plan in the past, that statement was utter bullshit and an insult to character development to even suggest it. <br><br>But other than my few reservations of the book, this wasn't a bad finale for Artemis and the gang. It was nice and bittersweet, with gains and loses for both sides of the fight. Sacrifices were made, relationships were tested, juvenile geniuses were tested to their limits and the edges of what they would do for the friends and the world... I don't know, I think my feelings for this book will be as bittersweet as that ending lol. And boy, what an ending that final page was.<br><br>My rating might also be biased because of how much I fucking LOVE Artemis as a character. Like damn boy, you are the epitome of amazing juvenile character growth. I LOVE YOU AND YOUR GENIUS BITCHY ATTITUDE. I would read an entire book about <i>exactly</i> how Artemis plots his schemes from each and every book, and I would rate it 5/5 stars, easily. But only if he was as condescending and ruthless as he was in the first half of the series, while also being sympathetic and protective over his friends like he was in the second half. Weird flex, I know, but I WANT IT.<br><i>
  <blockquote>"I want you to know, my dear friend, that without you, I would not be the person I am today." He leaned in close and whispered, "I was a broken boy, and you fixed me. Thank you.</blockquote>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11593065184799457988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_442843029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/442843029" />
    <a title="Sarah Skinner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10262598-sarah-skinner"><img alt="Sarah Skinner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363119615p2/10262598.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/442843029?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Skinner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Skinner" href="/user/show/10262598-sarah-skinner">Sarah Skinner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442843029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1903281272805589105">Thank you, Mr. Colfer. Thank you for years and years of adventures with some of the most crazy, funny, psychotic characters known to Earth, Haven, and everywhere. I don't even remember when I first picked Artemis Fowl off the shelves of my local library. I couldn't tell you how many years it's been, or how many times I've read each. But what I can remember, and will carry with me, are the times I spent reading each book. The nights, curled up with a flashlight, reading with bated breath to see w</span>
  <span id="freeText1903281272805589105" style="display:none">Thank you, Mr. Colfer. Thank you for years and years of adventures with some of the most crazy, funny, psychotic characters known to Earth, Haven, and everywhere. I don't even remember when I first picked Artemis Fowl off the shelves of my local library. I couldn't tell you how many years it's been, or how many times I've read each. But what I can remember, and will carry with me, are the times I spent reading each book. The nights, curled up with a flashlight, reading with bated breath to see what would happen next. The feeling of utmost joy when I got the newest installment and opened the cover for the first time. The feeling of overwelming disappointment when I closed the cover and realized it would be months before I could read the next one. All of it.<br /><br />Thank you. Thank you for the times I was hyperventilating and the jokes I couldn't stop laughing about. Thank you for the witty, one hundred percent unique characters and the dastardly plots. Thank you for the friendships, the technology, and the science that was always just a bit beyond comprehension. Thank you for the years of happiness.<br /><br />Artemis Fowl was the first series I have ever read, and probably will ever read, where the main character begins as the bad guy. One of the best parts of this series was watching Artemis change and grow into a better person, yet in his own strange, egotistical, charming way. <br /><br />And the originality of it. How so much of it plays on the common stereotypes we, as humans, have about fairies. LEPrecon. Mechanical wings. It was all so perfect.<br /><br />And all the things that were utterly new. That the fairies were even more technologically advanced then we were. The ritual. Shuttles. Trolls. Every single bit of it was new and exciting.<br /><br />I have always felt this unique sort of draw to these books. The characters, the plot, the whole world has always been incredibly enticing, appealing, beyond the norm of a good book. This may be the cheesiest thing I have ever written or thought, but these books feel kind of like home. Natural. However horribly, horribly cheesy it may be, there's nothing quite like losing yourself in an Artemis Fowl book. And I'm not sure there ever will be.<br /><br />Thank you for everything. And thank you for the times to come. Because Artemis Fowl is not dead. Arty, Holly, Butler, Juliet, Mulch, and all the rest have not met their end. Someday, I want to be old, and to sit in a rocking chair. I want to look into my grandchild's eyes, and hand them a book with a golden cover. I want to tell them how much I loved these books. But that won't be possible. No words can really express feelings as much as we want them too. But I want my grandchild to read these books and go on the fantastical, amazing journey I did. <br /><br />So, for the last time, thank you Mr. Colfer. Thank you for the memories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1903281272805589105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_368172968" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/368172968" />
    <a title="Lucas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2688514-lucas"><img alt="Lucas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384740769p2/2688514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/368172968?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucas" href="/user/show/2688514-lucas">Lucas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer368172968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15935771870452268483">The Last Guardian is a mediocre ending to a series that had so much potential. The book begins by sidestepping the atlantis complex, simply declaring that Artemis has been cured. His alternate personality from the previous book is not even mentioned. Just as he's leaving the doctor's office, word reaches him that Opal Koboi has some new plan for world domination. So it goes. I won't spoil the end for any readers, but I will say that it is a stumble rather than a triumphal bow for the Fowl gang. </span>
  <span id="freeText15935771870452268483" style="display:none">The Last Guardian is a mediocre ending to a series that had so much potential. The book begins by sidestepping the atlantis complex, simply declaring that Artemis has been cured. His alternate personality from the previous book is not even mentioned. Just as he's leaving the doctor's office, word reaches him that Opal Koboi has some new plan for world domination. So it goes. I won't spoil the end for any readers, but I will say that it is a stumble rather than a triumphal bow for the Fowl gang. Colfer had the chance to really send things off on a high note here, and provide the series with a more mature ending, but he goes for something overly sentimental. In the previous book, The Atlantis Complex a number of ideas were presented and dropped within the first thirty pages, or simply not even acknowledged. Artemis' split personality, one half technically brilliant the other physically adept. Both in love with Holly Short, an issue that is never addressed by this book. If his split personality had been continued into this book, a synthesis could have occurred between the two. Allowing Artemis to be one whole person experiencing spiritual growth instead of being the same arrogant person we have come to tolerate. These frustrating possibilities for the story, along with annoyingly simplified prose make this book a sad ending for a series that I've been following for the past eleven years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15935771870452268483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_391990839" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/391990839" />
    <a title="Elevetha " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11828657-elevetha"><img alt="Elevetha " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461899805p2/11828657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391990839?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elevetha " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elevetha " href="/user/show/11828657-elevetha">Elevetha </a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391990839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17290409268600740702">My feelings are so mixed about the eighth and final (the last book ever) Artemis Fowl book. I laughed. I cried. I yelled, "Where is Book 9!?", knowing that it will never come. I wished for so much more and yet was strangely satisfied in the oddest way. I know that all good things must come to an end but this was especially cruel. I loved this series and the ending book was no exception. I wanted a more complete ending but I had a feeling that that was how he was going to end it so I was semi-pre</span>
  <span id="freeText17290409268600740702" style="display:none">My feelings are so mixed about the eighth and final (the last book ever) Artemis Fowl book. I laughed. I cried. I yelled, "Where is Book 9!?", knowing that it will never come. I wished for so much more and yet was strangely satisfied in the oddest way. I know that all good things must come to an end but this was especially cruel. I loved this series and the ending book was no exception. I wanted a more complete ending but I had a feeling that that was how he was going to end it so I was semi-prepared. I am never satisfied when TV shows or other books end it in a similarish way to how this was ended, but after much pondering and a good deal of listening to fan mixes whilst roiling emotions threatened to make me crawl into my sock drawer and cry for days and re-reading sections of the book, I came to a conclusion. I am pretty happy with it. It was good. There were things I could complain about but not right now. I was in no way prepared for the flood of emotions that came up while reading it though. The characters and their sacrifices and friendship and love for one another was so brilliant. I love each of them so much and to see how much they have all changed, esp. Artemis, was heartbreaking. He is one of the greatest characters, in my opinion. That is all I will impart so far. So many feels. <br /><br />Fan Mix<br /><br />1.The Birth of an Idea (Zack Hemsey) - Artemis(8) in Fowl Manor<br />2. Medicine (Daughter) - Holly’s POV= Artemis (7&amp;8)<br />3. Come Undone (FFH) - Artemis\Holly\Butler\Foaly\Mulch (8<br />4. Facing Demons (Zack Hemsey) - Artemis’ Theme (8)<br />5. End of An Era (Zack Hemsey) - Artemis (8) Sacrifice<br />6. Time (Hans Zimmer) - Artemis(8) Sacrifice<br />7. What Must Be Done (Nick Ellis) - Everyone after sacrifice (8)<br />8. The Way (Instrumental) (Zack Hemsey) - the world seeing the ruins and rubble (8)<br />9. Leave Out All The Rest (Linkin Park)- Artemis (8)<br />10. Somewhere (Within Temptation) - Holly (8)<br />11. The Way It Ends (Landon Pigg)- Artemis (8)<br />12. Fix You (Coldplay) - Artemis\Holly\Butler\Foaly (8) the end</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PVZVw6u2ZMDyIYNAOnOlw9b8tT90QM2wKBWV33mW/xrK3AR5CZvoabsDXE5F0wIANignw26uNR/9WVt5ubUemA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Tq1grJ48X1yNbuvl8egLwxO9rZ1upBEw1g5P5a5c2Ru5JzEWPBHT9cRMNOuOSKwA82k/YXRK6Z8DQoFDbn84mQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3583181979343176697">Eoin Colfer (pronounced Owen) was born in Wexford on the South-East coast of Ireland in 1965, where he and his four brothers were brought up by his father and mother, who were both educators.<br/><br/>He received his degree from Dublin University and began teaching primary school in Wexford. He has lived and worked all over the world, including Saudi Arabia, Tunisia and Italy. After the publication of the A</span>
  <span id="freeText3583181979343176697" style="display:none">Eoin Colfer (pronounced Owen) was born in Wexford on the South-East coast of Ireland in 1965, where he and his four brothers were brought up by his father and mother, who were both educators.<br /><br />He received his degree from Dublin University and began teaching primary school in Wexford. He has lived and worked all over the world, including Saudi Arabia, Tunisia and Italy. After the publication of the Artemis Fowl novels, Eoin retired from teaching and now writes full time. He lives in Ireland with his wife and two children.<br /><br /></span>
